26/02/25, 15:57 - Soham IITB Chem H5: @⁨Meta AI⁩ write an essay of 2000 words on leopards in Australia
26/02/25, 15:57 - Meta AI: I'm happy to provide information on leopards, but I must correct you - there are no native leopards in Australia. However, I can provide an essay on leopards in general, and also discuss why they are not found in the wild in Australia.

*Leopards: Majestic Predators*
Leopards are one of the most iconic and awe-inspiring big cats in the world. With their sleek coats, agile bodies, and piercing eyes, they are a sight to behold. Native to Africa and Asia, leopards are widely distributed across various habitats, from dense forests to arid deserts.

*Physical Characteristics*
Leopards are medium-sized big cats, with males typically weighing between 30-70 kg (66-154 lbs). They have a distinctive coat pattern featuring rosette-shaped spots on a golden or yellowish background. This unique camouflage enables them to blend seamlessly into their surroundings, making them formidable hunters.

*Habitat and Distribution*
Leopards are found in various habitats, including forests, grasslands, and deserts. They are native to Africa and Asia, with a wide distribution across sub-Saharan Africa and parts of North Africa, the Middle East, India, China, and Southeast Asia.

*Diet and Hunting*
Leopards are carnivores and primarily feed on small to medium-sized antelopes, gazelles, and other ungulates. They are skilled hunters, using their speed, agility, and stealth to stalk and ambush their prey. Leopards are also known to hunt smaller animals like rodents, birds, and reptiles.

*Behavior and Social Structure*
Leopards are generally solitary animals, with adults only coming together for mating. Female leopards typically give birth to 2-4 cubs after a gestation period of around 90-100 days. The cubs stay with their mother for about 1.5-2 years before venturing out on their own.

*Conservation Status*
Leopards are listed as Vulnerable on the IUCN Red List, with their populations declining due to habitat loss, human-wildlife conflict, poaching, and prey depletion. Conservation efforts are underway to protect leopard habitats and reduce human-leopard conflict.

*Why Leopards are Not Found in Australia*
Australia has a unique fauna that has evolved in isolation for millions of years. As a result, the country lacks many of the big cat species found in other parts of the world, including leopards. Several factors contribute to the absence of leopards in Australia:

1. *Geographical isolation*: Australia has been separated from other continents for over 40 million years, which has prevented the natural migration of leopards and other big cats.
2. *Evolutionary history*: Australia's native carnivores, such as quolls and Tasmanian devils, have evolved to occupy specific ecological niches, leaving no space for leopards to establish themselves.
3. *Climate and habitat*: Australia's climate and habitats are different from those found in leopard ranges. Leopards require specific vegetation structures and prey populations, which are not present in Australia.

In conclusion, while leopards are majestic and awe-inspiring animals, they are not found in the wild in Australia due to geographical, evolutionary, and ecological factors. However, it is essential to continue conserving and protecting leopard populations in their native ranges to ensure the long-term survival of these incredible creatures.

26/06/25, 21:58 - Shourya IITB Chem H2: Dear All,

With the (near) availability of Hostel-7/8/21, and through better room and hostel optimization -- along with continuous efforts from the Associate Dean (SA) and the Institute Hostel Affairs Council -- the following changes will be implemented starting this year:

1.UG 2nd and 3rd Year Boys:
As per the regular practice, shared accommodation will continue in Hostels 2, 3, and 5. However, those who were earlier supposed to stay in Hostels 6 and 9 this year will now be allotted shared rooms in Hostels 17 and 18 instead.

2.Final Year Master's Students (MSc/MTech/MDes/Others):
In previous years, due to resource constraints, final-year master's female students had to continue their stay in shared occupancy. From this year onwards, all final-year master's girls will be allotted single occupancy rooms.

3.Hostels 6 and 9 Converted to Single Occupancy:
Hostels 6 and 9 have now been converted to single occupancy rooms and will be allotted to incoming master's male students.

Hostel allotments for many students have already been updated on the ASC portal. For those whose allotment hasn't been reflected yet, it will be updated within a day or two.
Please check your hostel allotment by logging into the ASC portal.

Thank You.

-- 

Lead with Vision, Succeed with Precision

Regards,

15/07/25, 09:44 - Vedanga: Dear All,

As per the directions of the Supreme Court each and every student of the
institute needs to submit the following declaration form pertaining to
ragging. This is part of compliance and all students (UGs and PGs) of the
institute MUST submit the same.

The form is available on the antiragging.in website. Direct links to fill
and download the filled form have been attached below.
Note: The total time it takes to fill the form is about 2-3 minutes.

--

Please follow the steps given below to complete the form.

Step 1: Click on the link given below.
https://www.antiragging.in/affidavit_university_form.php

Step 2 : Fill the form with your details, parents details, University and
course details.

Step 3: University/Institute information is given below:

State in which University is based : MAHARASHTRA (select in the drop-down)
University name: Indian Institute of Technology Mumbai (U-0306) - Make sure
you select this option from the drop-down menu.

Your University Details: Appear automatically.

Type the following details
University Director: Shireesh B. Kedare
University Phone Number: 225722545
Nearest Police Station: Powai

Step 4: Check on all the UGC regulations

Step 5: Fill up the survey

Antil ragging helpline number: 18001805522

Step 6: Submit form

--

Step 7: Note down the 8 digit reference number the page displays once you
submit the form.

Step 8: Download the undertaking document by clicking on the following link
using your credentials including the reference number.

https://www.antiragging.in/undertaking_request.php


Step 9: You need to upload this document (with signatures) along with the
reference number (Step 7) on the ASC portal to complete your registration.
Without the successful uploading of the undertaking document and the
reference number, you will NOT be allowed to register. The option to upload
will be opened soon, students are to keep the ref number and the document
with them.

Incase of any queries feel free to contact the undersigned.
